<user_id>103761656919622876467<//user_id>< Text>
This is your classic sports bar with lots of TVs, burgers and fries and an array of cold beer - mostly domestic.  I had the Patty Melt with tater tots and it was just what I expected.  A previously frozen patty grilled on the flattop.  The food was typical for a sports bar and I would give the somewhat limited menu 3 stars, so if you came just for the food there are better options in Redding.

As far as the sports bar aspect, they have that pretty well covered.  This is a popular place when a "big game" is playing.  There are also pool tables, a video jukebox, and a shuffleboard game.

I heard that an employee is the process of purchasing this bar.  Rumor is that he intends on keeping it a sport bar.  Hopefully the food will be improved.< /Text>

<Text>Stopped in for breakfast üç≥ü•ì on Jan. 20 2020 (MLK Day) and so thankful we did. We were greeted and seated right away and our drink order was promptly taken and delivered. I have to say the staff and service was on point. Our timing couldn't have been better as the place filled up and people were waiting, soon after we arrived.

We started our morning with hazelnut and vanilla lattes. For sustenance I ordered the carnitas chilaquiles, the wife had toads in the hole, and our beautiful and gracious pal-along, Sarah, ordered a short stack and hash browns.

Everything was terrific! Even all the steamy aromatic dishes on our neighboring tables looked amazingly delicious! Our food was delivered in a more-than- reasonable amount of time, it was hot, well portioned, and well plated.

I dove right in like an undisciplined parolee who had just gotten his first meal on the outside. All manners and discipline went out the door. It was a blur of egg yolk, carnitas, chips, and cheese. If this was a cage match it would have been over early in the first round. I had my meal in a rear naked choke hold; üíÄ that plate was cleared, cleaned & tapped out! ü§ò

When I came out of my fugazi, I looked up to find everybody was looking at me in bewilderment, amazement, and disgust üò©. I sat back is yolk dribbled from my chin under my shirt with a slight smile and 1/2 open eyes, in a state of Nirvana.

I used the washroom to make myself presentable. Got the check and paid, then we were off. All the tables were full as well as the 12-person counter seating, people were waiting outside. Parking lot was full and people were waiting to find a spot. Even though most of the businesses were closed for the holiday.

<Time>1453238243685</Time>< review>
Wow, what a difference from the old Farmer Boy.  I am thrilled that this restaurant kept some of the old style diner decorations from the old Farmer Boy.  The menu is smaller yet the food and menu are more quality driven. The prices are affordable and the ambiance is fresh, clean and uplifting.  The personnel are extremely friendly and treat you like family.  I highly recommend this "local's" restaurant to anyone wanting that "old" diner experience.  They open for dinner starting tonight and can't wait to experience their dinner menu. Thumbs up for the new Farmer Boy!

In response to the "one star" by one diner...I would think that you would be appreciative that the staff was willing to make you some 'fresh lemonade" to order.  Maybe not all that great, however, I don't think that kind of service doesn't warrant a "one star".  Just saying.</review>

< Text>
To other lone diners and first timers, like myself:

Grab a comfy, black leather swivel stool at the counter and order yourself some Chicken and Waffles. Whoever imagined adding chili flakes to the maple syrup....... Genius. It gives the sweet and savory dish an unexpectedly delicious heat.

And the service was great. The waitress always kept my coffee cup full and took time during refills to talk to me since she had never seen me dine at Farmer Boy before.
Although I dined alone, I never felt by myself. Thank you, awesome waitress. See you at the counter.</Text>

Burgers, made to order, were cooked exactly as we had ordered them.  Onion rings are homemade with a panko breading. The wings, were full wings, not just a section, and huge. The sauce wasn't to spicy that you couldn't eat them. Served with real blue cheese. The Cobb salad was made with romaine lettuce not cheap ass iceberg. Plenty of meat, egg, & tomato on it as well. Our waiter, Nick, was as friendly and accommodating as a guy could get. He even recommended beer choices for each of us.  We're typically Budlight and Mich Ultra fans and don't know anything about craft beers.  The place was clean, friendly and served REAL, good tasting food at a great price!  Us folks from the Midwest would definitely eat here again if we find ourselves in Santa Barbara again.</review>< pictures>

<name>David Rachford<//name><time>1450745689063< /time>< Rate>
4</Rate>
< review>
This is not the old Farmer Boy, and that's a good thing. Back in the day, I was served sour orange juice and cottage cheese past it's prime. Now, ingredients are fresh, flavorful and service is snappy.

Worth mentioning: Chilequiles are very good. I think I could make a case that Farmer Boy's Chilequeles are some of the best in town if you like carnitas (pork) with them. While I think the Boat House chilequeles win for presentation & visual appeal, their chilequeles are lacking in the pork department. Farmer Boy is more generous with the pork. The salsa has a slight tang that I like. Will definitely have them again. One minor issue, poached eggs ordered soft, one was medium one was firm. Not a big deal on a busy day, but a little room for improvement there.

Service was prompt & courteous; the staff truly works well as a team, they all seem to have each other's back. Our server Nise was on point during our busy Saturday breakfast. When a large party was taking her time, another server helped deliver drinks & kept things moving.

The family that runs this joint (along with Brophy's) knows service & good food keep people coming back.

I have one suggestion for improvement. The place is LOUD when full. The back room has an acoustic panel on the ceiling to help attenuate noise; unfortunately it's not enough. I suggest changing the artwork to prints on acoustic panels vs. the epoxy alumninum or fiberglass photo prints... although the artwork is pretty, it makes everyone's voice ricochet off the walls and for me, it's unpleasantly noisy for this diner on a busy day.

It's good to see this restaurant back in a much "new and improved" state.<//review>
